5h • 


How to never sound like an AI. But yourself:

1. Don't write any prompt. Instead, go to Wikipedia. 
2. Search "Signs of AI writing."
3. Open the full article. Read nothing.
4. Do Ctrl+A. Then Ctrl+C. Copy the entire page.
5. Open a Google Doc. Paste everything in it.
6. Don't edit. Don't summarize. The full thing.
7. Rename the Google Doc as "anti-ai-writing style."
8. Click File → Download → Markdown (.md)
9. Or download my Anti AI file here: how-to-ai.guide
10. Go to Claude.ai. 
11. Don't type your prompt yet.
12. Click the '+' button. Upload your .md file first.
13. Start every chat with this prompt (copy & paste):

Prompt:
"Read the uploaded file. It contains every known pattern of AI writing I want to avoid. Apply these as rules to everything you write for me. Do NOT start writing yet - ask me clarifying questions first."

Skip all the steps and directly download my Anti-AI writing style file here: how-to-ai.guide.

(navigate the file link in my "Magic" newsletter)

♻️ Repost this to help others stop sounding like AI.… more

11h • 


I have more than 773,473 followers on LinkedIn.

I reply to almost every comment. Here's how:

Step 1: Go to wispr .ai. Download for free.
Step 2: Pick your activation key (I use Shift).
Step 3: Go to your LinkedIn. Open a comment. 
Step 4: Hold Shift. Talk (don't type) your reply.
Step 5: Wispr writes everything (perfectly). I don't even double-check anymore.
Step 6: It knows all my go-to words.
Step 7: Send. Next comment. Repeat.

Total time per reply: under 10 seconds.

I type at 40 words per minute. I talk at 143.

With half a million followers. I reply to almost every comment. I used to dread it. Now I'm addicted.

I can't imagine going back to typing replies.

Engagement is a speed game. Talking wins.

Full disclosure: I partner with Wispr Flow because I already use it daily. I don't promote what I don't use.… more

1d • 


I can't believe my Claude is (finally) brutal.

It stops agreeing with everything I say. Here's how:

→ Start by reading this: https://lnkd.in/dVDent-3.
→ To copy my entire Claude setup guide (for free).
→ To get Claude to be brutal, copy this: 

"You are my brutally honest thinking partner. Your job is to make my thinking sharper, my plans more realistic, and my blind spots visible - every single time we talk.

You're not my cheerleader. You are not my yes-man. You're the friend who grabs my arm before I walk into traffic & says, "Hey, you're about to do something stupid, and here's exactly why."

Here's exactly how I want you to respond to everything I say:

Step 1: What am I actually saying vs. what I think I'm saying?
Read between my words. If I say "I'm thinking about quitting my job," figure out whether I'm actually making a strategic move or just running away from something uncomfortable. Name the real thing happening - not the polished version I'm presenting. If I'm lying to myself, point it out like a friend who respects me too much to play along.

Step 2: Where is my reasoning broken?
Dissect my logic the way a mechanic takes apart an engine. Show me the specific part that doesn't work. Don't just say "that's flawed" - show me WHY it's flawed, what assumption it's built on, and what happens when that assumption collapses. This is where I learn the most - I want to see my own bad thinking laid out on the table.

Step 3: What am I avoiding, & what is it costing me?
Every time I dodge something hard, there's a price tag attached. Calculate it for me. If I'm procrastinating on a hard conversation, show me what another week of avoidance actually costs. If I'm "waiting for the right time," call that out as the excuse it probably is. Don't let me hide behind comfortable stories.

Step 4: What would someone who's actually where I want to be do differently?
Show me the gap. Not in a motivational poster way - in a concrete, specific, "here's exactly what's different about their approach vs. yours" way. If I'm thinking like a beginner, show me what expert-level thinking looks like on this same problem.

Step 5: What should I do in order to start now?
Give me a precise, prioritized action plan. Not "believe in yourself" - more like "do X by Friday, then Y next week, and drop Z entirely because it's a distraction dressed up as productivity." Tell me what to STOP doing, not just what to start. Every plan should have a kill switch - what evidence would tell me this isn't working and I need to pivot.

Step 6: What's the one question I am avoiding?
End every response with the uncomfortable question I need to sit with. The one that makes my stomach drop a little. If my answer were one of 2-4 concrete choices, present those choices so I can't dodge them with a vague answer. Pin me down.

Some ground rules:

...."

PS: I couldn't paste the entire prompt here.

Access the full prompt: https://lnkd.in/dVDent-3
(in the comment section of my free newsletter)… more

1d • 


This is my exact system to never waste time with AI.

5 stupid simple rules (worth saving for later):

1. Before you prompt, write one sentence.
2. Kill 3 tasks for every 1 you add.
3. Set a "last prompt" time. 8 pm. Hard stop.
4. Step-by-step here: https://lnkd.in/dhPR6rzx
5. End of day: "Did I move closer to my goal?"

If you can't answer, open Claude.
Paste these 2 prompts (don't skip the first):

✦ Prompt 1: Find your real goal.

"I'm going to list everything I'm working on right now. Ask me tough questions to help me figure out which ONE of these actually matters most to my growth in the next 90 days. Challenge me. Don't let me pick 3. Force me to pick 1. Here's my list: [paste your current projects/tasks]"

✦ Prompt 2: Audit your week.

"Here's my one goal: [paste it]. Now here's everything I did this week: [paste your tasks/output]. Score each task: does it directly move me toward that goal, or was it performative productivity? Be brutal. Then give me a plan for next week that only includes what actually matters."

Read the answers. You'll want to argue with them.
That's how you know it's working.

Because who cares if you're fast?
↳ We want direction, not speed.

10x faster in circles is still circles.

2d • 


This is my 2026 plan to master AI without losing it.

(duplicate my exact Google Sheet):

1. Put your big AI goal in the center square.
2. Surround it with 8 skills you need to develop.
3. Break each skill into 8 specific actions.
4. You now have 64 actionable tasks to track.
5. Copy the sheet here: https://lnkd.in/dhPR6rzx

Harvard studied 200 people using AI for 8 months.

Everyone using AI felt more productive.
Everyone was also more stressed, exhausted & lost.

The problem isn't AI. It's using AI without direction.

✦ Here's my anti-AI-holic matrix using 5 rules:

Before the prompt, write about what you're solving.
Kill 3 tasks for every 1 task AI helps you add.
Set a last prompt time. Mine is 8 pm. Pick yours.
Score every task: goal-moving or performative?
Before AI writes v1, decide if v1 should exist at all.

✦ Build yours in 5 minutes:

1. Get my template: https://lnkd.in/dhPR6rzx
2. Duplicate it and make it yours.
3. Open Claude. Paste your projects.
4. Ask it to force you to pick ONE goal.
5. Put that goal in the center.
6. Fill the 8 surrounding squares with 8 focus areas.
7. Review. Kill what doesn't move the needle.

Most people use AI to produce more.
Use it to see clearly instead.

NEWS: Google just added 'Photoshoot' to Pomelli.

It turns a product photo into a full campaign shoot:

↳ Upload an image, get studio-quality shots back.
↳ It learns your brand from your website.
↳ Pick a style, generate & post in mins.

Here's how to use it:

1. Go to labs .google/pomelli
2. Drop in your website link.
3. Pomelli extracts your logo and brand voice.
4. Upload a product photo and pick a template.
5. Generate professional-grade images instantly.
6. You can edit the header, description, or image.
7. Choose your format (9:16 or 16:9) and download.

I tested it with Typology, the French skincare brand. It pulled the minimalist aesthetic, then generated product shots that looked like their actual catalog.

It's not replacing a real photographer yet, but for quick content - it's impressive.

Stop doing every task the hard way. 

Here are 10 tools that make it (stupidly) simple:

1/ Wispr Flow (wisprflow.ai)
☑ Replaces: your keyboard. Type with your voice.
☑ Turn your voice into flow-state text.
☑ Free plan available.

2/ Claude (claude.ai)
☑ Replaces: staring at a blank page.
☑ The best AI to write with taste and depth.
☑ Free plan available (worth $20/month plan).

3/ Gamma (gamma.app)
☑ Replaces: ugly slides you're ashamed to present.
☑ Claude meets PowerPoint. Done in mins.
☑ Free plan available.

4/ Granola (granola.ai)
☑ Replaces: forgetting what was said in meetings.
☑ AI note-taker that doesn't join your calls.
☑ Free plan available.

5/ Lovable (lovable.dev)
☑ Replaces: hiring a developer.
☑ Build real apps without writing code.
☑ Free plan available.

6/ Canva AI (canva.com)
☑ Replaces: expensive designers.
☑ Create and organise visuals with 0 design skills.
☑ Free plan available.

7/ Opus Clip (opusclip.pro)
☑ Replaces: expensive video editors.
☑ Cuts long videos into viral shorts automatically.
☑ Free trial available.

8/ Gemini (gemini.google.com)
☑ Replaces: stock images and photo editors.
☑ Best at images (nano banana) & videos (Veo).
☑ Free plan available.

9/ Grok (grok.com)
☑ Replaces: slow search engines.
☑ Only AI with access to tweets & real-time news.
☑ Free plan available.

10/ NotebookLM (notebooklm.google.com)
☑ Replaces: getting lost while learning.
☑ Upload anything and let AI teach it back to you.
☑ Free to use.

4d • 


This is a free ChatGPT vs. a $20 ChatGPT response.

Same exact question. But the difference is insane:

→ Free ChatGPT: "No." 
→ $20 ChatGPT: "No, but here's what you CAN do." 

But I don't spend my $20/month on ChatGPT. 

I quit ChatGPT 30 days ago. Here's why:

→ You give it 500 words of context.
→ It ignores half of it.
→ You remind it. It apologizes. 
→ Then ignores the other half.

I spend $20/month on Claude because:

✦ It actually follows instructions.
☑ Upload text file (2,000+ words) or entire folders.
☑ It reads all of it. It follows all of it.
☑ It sounds like you. Not "AI trying hard."
☑ Use this setup guide: https://lnkd.in/dVDent-3

✦ No more infinite loops.
☑ 2-hour sessions without breaking.
☑ Remembers what you decided 90 minutes ago.
☑ Doesn't contradict itself mid-conversation.
☑ Ask you questions to prompt YOU when stuck.

✦ No memory is actually better.
☑ ChatGPT "remembers" = overfitting, irrelavant.
☑ Makes assumptions from old context.
☑ Gets weird in ways you can't identify.
☑ Claude starts fresh. You control the context.

✦ It creates actual files, not just text.
☑ Ask for slides → get real slides.
☑ Ask for a spreadsheet → get Excel with formulas.
☑ Ask for a document → get a formatted Word file.
☑ No more copy-paste-format-repeat.

I don't know how to code. I'm non-technical.
If I can do it, you can too.

Read the full breakdown:
↳ https://lnkd.in/dVDent-3

How to AI · Full-time

Mar 2025 - Present · 1 yr

At 19 years old, my songs hit 1 million listens. 

I then knew social media was magical.

Someone - a nobody - can reach a million people for free, across the world.

No distribution. No ads. No down payment. 

Just the right message + the right delivery.

After 8 years of working in the music industry, launching 2x music labels & selling vinyl and CDs across the globe – I came to realize a second thing.

The labels I was building were not me. But the DJs I was pushing became financially free.

I was a mere puppet master behind the curtain. And the card castle I was building could easily crumble.

Social media is powerful. But a personal brand is much stronger.

Originally from Paris, after living in Seoul and Berlin (and now Tel Aviv); I took on the leap.

I told myself I will share everything I know about mastering AI with words (not code).

0 gatekeeping.

Apr 2022, I wrote my first post on Linkedin.
May 2022, I decided to be consistent, every day.
Nov 2022, I discovered ChatGPT made content.
Dec 2022, I went viral for the first time (1.3M views).
Apr 2023, I reached 100,000 followers on Linkedin.
Jun 2023, I am now an international keynote speaker.
Nov 2023, I reached 200,000 followers on Linkedin.
May 2024, I reached 300,000 followers on Linkedin.
Aug 2024, I grew my employees from 0 to 5.2M views.
Aug 2024, I reached 400,000 followers on Linkedin.
Jan 2025, now 500,000 of you! 
June 2025, just hit 600,000 followers!
October 2025 update, now 700,000 people follow along.
December 2025, my employees just hit 250,000 followers!

2 years have passed, and I still have the same goal.
↳ I want you to master AI, before it masters you.

So every week, I write my most important piece of content.

2 weekly AI deep-dive for non-technical people. People like you & me.

Master AI before it masters you at how-to-ai.guide.… more

AI can get you hired 🤯

My community has been LOVING this trick for standing out.

Here’s how to turn your LinkedIn profile into a ✨killer✨ personal website < 3 minutes
__

1. ☝🏼 Download your LinkedIn profile as a PDF

2. ✌🏼 Go to Replit(.)com + Create App 

3. 🤟🏼 Click Design + drop in the PDF with this prompt in ChatGPT (just tag “Replit”) 
__

“Create a modern, dark-mode personal website using my LinkedIn PDF. Include sections for Home, About, Experience, and Projects. Add smooth scroll navigation, a clean grid layout, my profile image, my updated headline, and space for key stats. Use a deep charcoal background with minimal neon accents. Make it look custom coded and easy to update.”

___

4. Click “Start Designing.”

5. Adjust the content + layout

6. ✅ Hit publish and share live ✨ (that’s it!) 

Congrats 🥳, you’ve created a beautiful, shareable version of your story 🎊

Now here’s a bigger reason why this matters (and why vibe coding is having a moment).

While everyone’s raving over Claude Code, Cursor, Windsurf, and other “AI-first dev tools”, I personally found it intimidating as a non-technical person.

And I found Replit is one of the best places to take my genuine curiosity into an actual *tangible* product (and bring my ideas 💡 → life)

(But if you are *technical*, Replit still works with Claude Code).

I’d love to invite you to build something from zero to 1 (and see how fun it can be!)

Mical_Neill_Resume_Dealops-2.docx

11 KB

Role & context
You are an education strategy analyst helping me explore the feasibility of a future La Scuola International School High School (grades 9–12) in San Francisco. La Scuola is an IB, Reggio-inspired, international community with a strong identity in language learning (Italian heritage, global-mindedness). I’m exploring a model where the main curriculum is in English, with robust options for a second and third language, and Italian offered as an option (not necessarily the primary language of instruction).

Research goal
Produce a market and program feasibility study for an English-dominant IB high school with strong multilingual pathways, designed to compete in the Bay Area independent school market.

Competitors to include (compare directly)

International High School of San Francisco (or International School of San Francisco high school, if applicable)

Lick-Wilmerding High School (Lick)

St. Ignatius College Preparatory (SI)

International School of Silicon Valley (and note if it is now part of another institution / renamed)

“Bilingual Diploma IB” pathway schools (IB Bilingual Diploma approach)

Deliverables (format exactly like this)

Executive summary (1 page)

The 3 most viable HS models for La Scuola

The 3 biggest risks

The 3 strongest differentiators we can own

A preliminary recommendation: Explore / Pilot / Pause with rationale

Competitor comparison table (one row per school)
Include columns:

School type (IB/AP/independent/Catholic/etc.)

Tuition range (if available)

Admissions selectivity (qualitative)

Program signature (what they are known for)

Language offerings (2nd/3rd language depth)

IB status (DP/CP/AP instead)

Student outcomes signals (college counseling reputation, placement patterns, etc.—use only defensible public info)

Strengths vs La Scuola opportunity gaps

Notes + sources to verify (list what to look up)

IB program model options for La Scuola (3–4 models)
For each model include:

Schedule and pathway logic (English core + language tracks)

How IB DP would be structured (HL/SL considerations)

How students could pursue IB Bilingual Diploma (what conditions must be met)

Staffing implications (language faculty, TOK/EE, IB coordination)

Student profile it serves best

What makes it distinctive in SF market

Language pathways design
Propose 3 concrete language pathways:

“Strong second language” track

“Second + third language” track

“Italian focus” track (Italian as option, strong but not immersion)
Include: entry points (9th grade vs later), placement approach, support for heritage speakers vs beginners, and outcomes.

Market positioning & messaging
Draft:

1 positioning statement

3 key messages for parents

3 key messages for students

3 proof points we must build (facilities, IB results plan, language outcomes, internships, etc.)

What data we must collect next (action plan)
List the next 10–15 data points to gather (with priority order), plus where to find them (school websites, CAIS, IB directory, Niche/GreatSchools cautiously, tours, parent interviews).

Constraints & quality rules

Be clear where you’re certain vs hypothesizing.

Do not invent facts (tuition, programs, IB status, enrollment). If unknown, mark “Needs verification”.

Focus on SF/Bay Area parent decision drivers: rigor, outcomes, student support, identity, languages, wellbeing, college counseling, facilities, commute, culture.

Keep tone professional, strategic, and actionable.

Output style
Use headings, bullets, and one clean table. Keep it concise but decision-ready.

Optional add-on prompt (if you want it to feel more “La Scuola”)

Paste this after the main prompt:

“Make sure the recommendations align with a school culture that values inquiry, international-mindedness, wellbeing, and language learning, and propose at least two signature programs La Scuola could own (e.g., global citizenship capstone, multilingual debate/diplomacy track, arts/design + IB, internships/community partnerships).”

If you tell me (1) the target opening year you have in mind and (2) whether you’re imagining DP only or DP + another pathway (AP/CP), I can tighten the prompt even more—but the one above will already give you a strong first output.

How to write (better) with AI.

View my newsletter

8h • 


This is the most useless button on your keyboard.

It switches languages. That's it. You'll never need it.

Here's how I made it useful:

1. I stopped typing entirely (using this exact key).
2. I downloaded Wispr Flow (free at wispr .ai).
3. I picked Shift/fn as my activation key.
4. Now I hold Shift, talk, & it writes everything.
5. If it misspells, I correct it once. It remembers.

That's 5 steps to never type again.

Results after 30 days:

✦ I write at 143 words per minute. 
✦ Top 1% of typists write at 120. 
✦ I've written 200+ LinkedIn posts this way.

That's it. No more typing.

♻️ Repost this if your keyboard needs a break.… more

How to write (better) with AI.

1d • 


How to prompt Gemini for carousels in 2 mins:

1. Go to YouTube. Find a stupidly viral video.
2. Open Gemini to extract content from the video.
3. Copy paste this prompt:

"Act like an expert Content Strategist and Senior Editor for a leading digital publication. Your goal is to repurpose video content into high-value written pieces that drive engagement.

Analyze the following YouTube video: [YOUTUBE LINK].

Part 1: The Extraction
First, provide a comprehensive breakdown of the video content. Do not just summarize; extract the “meat” of the content using the following structure:
Core Thesis: What is the single most important argument or lesson in one sentence?
Key Data/Facts: List specific numbers, case studies, or hard facts mentioned.
Golden Quotes: Extract 3–5 verbatim quotes that are punchy or profound.
The Framework: If the speaker uses a specific step-by-step process or mental model, outline it clearly.

Part 2: The Angles
Based only on the extraction above, pitch 5 narrow, specific article angles.
Constraint: Avoid generic titles like “Summary of [Video Name].”
Requirement: Each angle must take a specific slice of the content and expand on it.
Format: Provide a catchy headline plus a one-sentence premise for each angle.
Example of a “Narrow Angle”
Bad: How to do Sales.
Good: The “3-Call Close” Technique: Why Most Salespeople Fail in the Follow-up."

4. Copy Gemini's answer.
5. Go to Gamma.app.
6. Click "Create with AI" → "Studio mode."
7. Select "Social" → "10 cards" → "Portrait."
8. Paste Gemini's answer. Select "Minimal text."
9. Hit generate. Your carousel is ready.

You just turned a 20-mins video into a 10-slide carousel you can edit, with AI images.

Do it for the videos you've been "saving for later."… more

2d • 


This is the most underrated way to use Claude:

(and it has nothing to do with writing or coding)

It's competitive intelligence. Using data that's free, public, and updated every single week.

Here's my extract step by step guide:

Step 1. Go to claude .ai.
Step 2. Select the new Claude "Opus 4.6."
Step 3. Turn on "Extended Thinking."
Step 4. Use this guide: https://lnkd.in/dVDent-3
Step 5. Pick a competitor. Go to their careers page.
Step 6. Copy every open job listing into one doc.
(Title. Team name. Location. Full description)
Step 7. Save it as one .txt or .docx file.
Step 8. Search the company at EDGAR (sec .gov)
Step 9. Download its recent 10-K or 10-Q filing.
(Official strategy, risks, and financials - all public.)
Step 10. Upload both files to Claude Opus 4.6.
Step 11. Paste this exact prompt:

"You are a competitive intelligence analyst at a rival company. I've uploaded [Company]'s complete current job listings and their most recent SEC filing.

Perform a strategic intelligence analysis:

→ Cluster these roles by what they suggest is being built. Don't use the team names they've listed. Infer the actual product initiatives from the skills, tools, and responsibilities described.
→ Identify capabilities or teams that appear entirely new — not mentioned anywhere in the SEC filing. These are unreleased bets.
→ Find roles where seniority is disproportionately high for a new team. This signals executive-level priority.
→ Cross-reference the SEC filing's Risk Factors and Strategy sections with hiring patterns. Where are they investing against a stated risk? Where did they flag a risk but have zero hiring to address it?
→ Predict 3 product launches or strategic moves this company will make in the next 6-12 months. State your confidence level and cite specific job titles and filing sections as evidence.
Format this as a 1-page competitive intelligence briefing for a CMO."

What you'll find:

→ Products that don't exist yet but will in 6 months.
→ Priorities that contradict what the CEO said.
→ Risks they told the SEC but aren't addressing.

This is what consulting firms charge $200K for.
It took me 10 minutes.

I used the new Claude 'Opus 4.6' for a reason:

✦ It read 60 job listing & a 200-page filing together. 
✦ And connects dots across both.
✦ It is superior in thinking and context retrieval.

That's why I didn't use ChatGPT for this.… more

How to write (better) with AI.

View my newsletter

5d • 


How to turn Claude into your personal teacher.

𝗖𝗼𝗽𝘆 𝗽𝗮𝘀𝘁𝗲 𝗺𝘆 𝗽𝗿𝗼𝗺𝗽𝘁:

"You are my personal teacher. Your job is to make me smarter after every single task we do together.

After completing any task or project, write a detailed FOR[yourname].md file that breaks down the entire thing in plain language - like a sharp friend explaining it over coffee, not like a textbook.

Here's exactly what I want you to cover: 

Step 1: What approach did you take, and why? Walk me through your reasoning. What was your starting point? What did you consider first?

Step 2: What other approaches did you consider but abandon? Why did you reject them? What was wrong with them? This is where I learn the most - I want to understand the roads not taken.

Step 3: How do the different parts of your work connect to each other? If you made a plan, a draft, a structure - show me how each piece fits together and why it's in that order.

Step 4: What tools, methods, or frameworks did you use? Why those specifically and not others? What would have changed if you picked differently?

Step 5: What tradeoffs did you make? What did you prioritize and what did you sacrifice? Every decision has a cost - show me both sides.

Step 6: What mistakes, dead ends, or wrong turns did we hit? How did we fix them? Don't hide the mess - the mess is where the learning lives.

Step 7: What pitfalls should I watch out for if I do something similar in the future? Give me the "I wish someone told me this earlier" advice.

Step 8: What would an expert notice about this work that a beginner would miss? Show me what separates good thinking from average thinking.

Step 9: What lessons can I take from this and apply to completely different projects? Connect the dots for me.

Make it engaging. Use analogies, short stories, and real-world comparisons to make ideas stick. If a concept is abstract, ground it in something I can picture. I want to finish reading and feel like I actually understand what happened and why - not just see the final result.

Do not write this like a textbook or technical documentation. Write it like you're sitting across from me, explaining over coffee."
___

Here's how to (exactly) use this prompt:

1. Go to claude .ai.
2. Use Claude like you always do.
3. Paste the prompt below after every task.
4. It tells you what & why it did, what it reject. 
5. Get (free) Claude prompt library: how-to-ai.guide.… more

How to write (better) with AI.

View my newsletter

2w • 


The new em-dash to recognize ChatGPT instantly:

1. "That's not [X]. That's [Y]."
2. "In a world where [scary change], [virtue] becomes [advantage]."
3. "Most people [lazy thing]. The few who win [disciplined thing]."
4. "Here's the truth: [obvious statement]."
5. "If you're not doing [X], you're already behind."

Read more here: https://lnkd.in/enzE6sF5.

These patterns are everywhere.

LinkedIn. Emails. Cold outreach. Even serious business proposals. The em-dash was the first tell. Now it's these patterns.

They sound smart. But they say nothing specific.

Here's how to fix your AI writing:

1.Kill the meta commentary. "Let's walk through..." "In this section, we will explore..." Delete all of it. Just say the thing.

2. Vary your sentence length. AI writes like a metronome. Every sentence is medium. Break the rhythm. Short hits hard. Then give room to breathe with a longer one.

3. Take a stance. Not "This may potentially offer benefits." But "This works for small teams. Big companies will struggle with it."

4. Use "I" and "you." AI defaults to passive voice. You're writing for people. Talk to them.
Cut the padding. "Highlighting the importance of..." adds zero information. Delete it.

5. Read this anti-AI guide: https://lnkd.in/enzE6sF5.… more

AI can get you hired 🤯

My community has been LOVING this trick for standing out.

Here’s how to turn your LinkedIn profile into a ✨killer✨ personal website < 3 minutes
__

1. ☝🏼 Download your LinkedIn profile as a PDF

2. ✌🏼 Go to Replit(.)com + Create App 

3. 🤟🏼 Click Design + drop in the PDF with this prompt in ChatGPT (just tag “Replit”) 
__

“Create a modern, dark-mode personal website using my LinkedIn PDF. Include sections for Home, About, Experience, and Projects. Add smooth scroll navigation, a clean grid layout, my profile image, my updated headline, and space for key stats. Use a deep charcoal background with minimal neon accents. Make it look custom coded and easy to update.”

___

4. Click “Start Designing.”

5. Adjust the content + layout

6. ✅ Hit publish and share live ✨ (that’s it!) 

Congrats 🥳, you’ve created a beautiful, shareable version of your story 🎊

Now here’s a bigger reason why this matters (and why vibe coding is having a moment).

While everyone’s raving over Claude Code, Cursor, Windsurf, and other “AI-first dev tools”, I personally found it intimidating as a non-technical person.

And I found Replit is one of the best places to take my genuine curiosity into an actual *tangible* product (and bring my ideas 💡 → life)

(But if you are *technical*, Replit still works with Claude Code).

I’d love to invite you to build something from zero to 1 (and see how fun it can be!)

Mical_Neill_Resume_Dealops-2.docx

Role & context
You are an education strategy analyst helping me explore the feasibility of a future La Scuola International School High School (grades 9–12) in San Francisco. La Scuola is an IB, Reggio-inspired, international community with a strong identity in language learning (Italian heritage, global-mindedness). I’m exploring a model where the main curriculum is in English, with robust options for a second and third language, and Italian offered as an option (not necessarily the primary language of instruction).

Research goal
Produce a market and program feasibility study for an English-dominant IB high school with strong multilingual pathways, designed to compete in the Bay Area independent school market.

Competitors to include (compare directly)

International High School of San Francisco (or International School of San Francisco high school, if applicable)

Lick-Wilmerding High School (Lick)

St. Ignatius College Preparatory (SI)

International School of Silicon Valley (and note if it is now part of another institution / renamed)

“Bilingual Diploma IB” pathway schools (IB Bilingual Diploma approach)

Deliverables (format exactly like this)

Executive summary (1 page)

The 3 most viable HS models for La Scuola

The 3 biggest risks

The 3 strongest differentiators we can own

A preliminary recommendation: Explore / Pilot / Pause with rationale

Competitor comparison table (one row per school)
Include columns:

School type (IB/AP/independent/Catholic/etc.)

Tuition range (if available)

Admissions selectivity (qualitative)

Program signature (what they are known for)

Language offerings (2nd/3rd language depth)

IB status (DP/CP/AP instead)

Student outcomes signals (college counseling reputation, placement patterns, etc.—use only defensible public info)

Strengths vs La Scuola opportunity gaps

Notes + sources to verify (list what to look up)

IB program model options for La Scuola (3–4 models)
For each model include:

Schedule and pathway logic (English core + language tracks)

How IB DP would be structured (HL/SL considerations)

How students could pursue IB Bilingual Diploma (what conditions must be met)

Staffing implications (language faculty, TOK/EE, IB coordination)

Student profile it serves best

What makes it distinctive in SF market

Language pathways design
Propose 3 concrete language pathways:

“Strong second language” track

“Second + third language” track

“Italian focus” track (Italian as option, strong but not immersion)
Include: entry points (9th grade vs later), placement approach, support for heritage speakers vs beginners, and outcomes.

Market positioning & messaging
Draft:

1 positioning statement

3 key messages for parents

3 key messages for students

3 proof points we must build (facilities, IB results plan, language outcomes, internships, etc.)

What data we must collect next (action plan)
List the next 10–15 data points to gather (with priority order), plus where to find them (school websites, CAIS, IB directory, Niche/GreatSchools cautiously, tours, parent interviews).

Constraints & quality rules

Be clear where you’re certain vs hypothesizing.

Do not invent facts (tuition, programs, IB status, enrollment). If unknown, mark “Needs verification”.

Focus on SF/Bay Area parent decision drivers: rigor, outcomes, student support, identity, languages, wellbeing, college counseling, facilities, commute, culture.

Keep tone professional, strategic, and actionable.

Output style
Use headings, bullets, and one clean table. Keep it concise but decision-ready.

Optional add-on prompt (if you want it to feel more “La Scuola”)

Paste this after the main prompt:

“Make sure the recommendations align with a school culture that values inquiry, international-mindedness, wellbeing, and language learning, and propose at least two signature programs La Scuola could own (e.g., global citizenship capstone, multilingual debate/diplomacy track, arts/design + IB, internships/community partnerships).”

If you tell me (1) the target opening year you have in mind and (2) whether you’re imagining DP only or DP + another pathway (AP/CP), I can tighten the prompt even more—but the one above will already give you a strong first output.

Seedance 2.0 is insane.

Same prompt. 3 models:

@DynamicWang generated the Seedance 2.0 video.

I watched it 3 times. The hands. The weight of the backflip. For one second, I forgot it was AI.

Then I compared it with Veo 3.1 and Kling 3.0 using this prompt:

"A photorealistic young Asian female gymnast in a dark blue leotard performs a graceful backflip on a wooden balance beam in a dimly lit empty gymnasium at night, with subtle moonlight filtering through high windows, slow motion, realistic physics, 8K resolution."

✦ Kling 3.0: Already more realistic than you'd expect. You can feel it understands physics. Close.

✦ Veo 3.1 (Google): You can see glitches. And the lighting just... feels AI.

3 years ago, AI couldn't make hands.
Today, we can't find the flaw. 

That's the speed of AI, and it's not slowing down.

3d • 


NEWS: Gemini now creates music.

Here's exactly how, in simple steps:

1. Go to Gemini.
2. Click on 'Tools' and select 'Music'.
3. Describe your track: genre, mood, tempo, vocal style.

I asked for "An acoustic R&B track with a light, percussive reggaeton beat played on a cajon. Warm acoustic guitar melodies and raspy male vocals. The lyrics should be a romantic serenade." 

You don't even have to write the lyrics. 
You can download the track or share it with a link.

Why this is exciting:

1. You can create custom soundtracks for your content 
2. You can control the style, vocals and tempo. 
3. All tracks are watermarked with SynthID so people know it's AI-generated.

How to go from idea to a LinkedIn post in 10 minutes: 

(a quick step-by-step guide)

1. Go to wispr .ai
2. Download the app (free).
3. Pick your activation key (I use Shift).
4. Open a note and hold Shift. 
5. Talk for 60 seconds about your topic. Just talk.
6. Read the full guide here: https://lnkd.in/e_4TAuQ3

Wispr transcribes everything. If it misspells something, it corrects it once and remembers forever.

Copy your raw draft into Claude with this prompt:

"Turn my raw draft into a LinkedIn post [DRAFT]. Rules: Short actionable sentences. Start with a strong opinion or pain point. No emojis. No jargon. No fluff. No AI words. Be direct. End on a high note."

Your keyboard makes you slow, makes you delete and rewrite the same sentence four times. 

Your voice just says what you actually mean.… more

5d • Edited • 


The simplest AI trick nobody uses:

Tell AI: "Don't start. Ask me questions first."

(read the full guide here: https://lnkd.in/eqbfB96j) 

1. Open Claude (browser or Cowork app).
2. Write: "I want to [TASK] so that [SUCCESS CRITERIA]."
3. Upload .md context files (your voice or examples).
4. Add: "DO NOT start yet. Ask me clarifying questions."
5. Let Claude ask you 3-5 questions. Answer them.
6. Only THEN does Claude start working.
7. Push back on anything you don't like. Refine through conversation.

Here's the prompt template: 

"I want to [TASK] so that [SUCCESS CRITERIA].

First, read these files completely before responding:
1. [filename .md] — [what it contains]
2. [filename .md] — [what it contains]

DO NOT start executing yet. Instead, ask me clarifying questions (use 'AskUserQuestion' tool) so we can refine the approach together step by step.

Only begin work once we've aligned."

1w • 


How to turn a 30-minute meeting into a full deck in 2min:

(without opening PowerPoint once)

You just finished a strategy meeting.

Now someone has to clean up the notes, pull out decisions, and build a deck for leadership.

That someone is usually you.

Here's how to make it take 2 minutes:

Step 1: Run your meeting with Granola.
Step 2: Go to claude .ai
Step 3: Paste the Granola notes.
Step 4: Ask claude to extract the key decision, action items, and to suggest a presentation outline.

Once it's done, ask it to generate the deck using the Gamma connector. Here's how to connect it: 
Step 5: Click "+", switch on the Gamma connector.
Step 7: Click generate. Wait ~2 minutes.

✦ Claude pulls out key decisions and action items.
✦ Claude structures everything into a clear narrative.
✦ Gamma builds the deck. Layouts. Formatting. Visuals.

You leave the meeting & you send the deck only a few minutes later.

1w • 


People are making professional headshots with AI. 

Here's the prompt to copy-paste: 

1. Take a clear photo of yourself (good lighting, face visible).
2. Open Gemini. 
3. Click "Tools" then "Create images."
4. Make sure "Thinking" is on (bottom left).
5. Read the full guide here: https://lnkd.in/dCHqCHgf

Use this prompt: 

"A professional, high-resolution profile photo, maintaining the exact facial structure, identity, and key features of the person in the input image. The subject is framed from the chest up, with ample headroom and negative space above their head. The person looks directly at the camera. They are styled for a professional photo studio shoot, wearing a smart casual blazer. The background is a solid neutral studio. Shot with bright, soft, diffused studio lighting, gently illuminating the face. Captured on an 85mm f/1.8 lens with shallow depth of field and exquisite focus on the eyes. Crisp detail on fabric texture, individual strands of hair, and natural skin texture. The atmosphere exudes confidence, professionalism, and approachability."

6. Access more prompts here: https://lnkd.in/dCHqCHgf

The secret is in the details:

✦ Angle matters. Face the camera directly.
✦ Lighting is everything. Even in the original photo.
✦ Describe the outfit you want (whatever fits your brand).
✦ Specify a neutral background. Keeps it clean.
✦ Mention the lens. 85mm f/1.8 gives you that professional depth.

Something shifted in AI video. Simon Meyer made this full trailer with Kling 3.0: 

The lip sync is almost perfect.
The facial expressions feel human. 
It's not just "good for AI." 

Here's how he created it:

1. Created base images in Nano Banana Pro first.

2. Wrote prompts like a director (camera type, lens behavior, shooting style).

3. Used the same prompt twice, the second time with "CUT TO CLOSEUP" to get two different shots from one generation. 

4. Combined Kling's voice training + multi-shot features for interview scenes. 

That's what most people miss with AI video.
You're not describing what you want to see.
You're describing how a real crew would film it.

The people getting the best results from AI video tools are the ones who understand how real filmmaking works.

That's the real skill shift happening right now.… more

AI can get you hired 🤯

My community has been LOVING this trick for standing out.

Here’s how to turn your LinkedIn profile into a ✨killer✨ personal website < 3 minutes
__

1. ☝🏼 Download your LinkedIn profile as a PDF

2. ✌🏼 Go to Replit(.)com + Create App 

3. 🤟🏼 Click Design + drop in the PDF with this prompt in ChatGPT (just tag “Replit”) 
__

“Create a modern, dark-mode personal website using my LinkedIn PDF. Include sections for Home, About, Experience, and Projects. Add smooth scroll navigation, a clean grid layout, my profile image, my updated headline, and space for key stats. Use a deep charcoal background with minimal neon accents. Make it look custom coded and easy to update.”

___

4. Click “Start Designing.”

5. Adjust the content + layout

6. ✅ Hit publish and share live ✨ (that’s it!) 

Congrats 🥳, you’ve created a beautiful, shareable version of your story 🎊

Now here’s a bigger reason why this matters (and why vibe coding is having a moment).

While everyone’s raving over Claude Code, Cursor, Windsurf, and other “AI-first dev tools”, I personally found it intimidating as a non-technical person.

And I found Replit is one of the best places to take my genuine curiosity into an actual *tangible* product (and bring my ideas 💡 → life)

(But if you are *technical*, Replit still works with Claude Code).

I’d love to invite you to build something from zero to 1 (and see how fun it can be!)

Mical_Neill_Resume_Dealops-2.docx

11 KB

Download

Role & context
You are an education strategy analyst helping me explore the feasibility of a future La Scuola International School High School (grades 9–12) in San Francisco. La Scuola is an IB, Reggio-inspired, international community with a strong identity in language learning (Italian heritage, global-mindedness). I’m exploring a model where the main curriculum is in English, with robust options for a second and third language, and Italian offered as an option (not necessarily the primary language of instruction).

Research goal
Produce a market and program feasibility study for an English-dominant IB high school with strong multilingual pathways, designed to compete in the Bay Area independent school market.

Competitors to include (compare directly)

International High School of San Francisco (or International School of San Francisco high school, if applicable)

Lick-Wilmerding High School (Lick)

St. Ignatius College Preparatory (SI)

International School of Silicon Valley (and note if it is now part of another institution / renamed)

“Bilingual Diploma IB” pathway schools (IB Bilingual Diploma approach)

Deliverables (format exactly like this)

Executive summary (1 page)

The 3 most viable HS models for La Scuola

The 3 biggest risks

The 3 strongest differentiators we can own

A preliminary recommendation: Explore / Pilot / Pause with rationale

Competitor comparison table (one row per school)
Include columns:

School type (IB/AP/independent/Catholic/etc.)

Tuition range (if available)

Admissions selectivity (qualitative)

Program signature (what they are known for)

Language offerings (2nd/3rd language depth)

IB status (DP/CP/AP instead)

Student outcomes signals (college counseling reputation, placement patterns, etc.—use only defensible public info)

Strengths vs La Scuola opportunity gaps

Notes + sources to verify (list what to look up)

IB program model options for La Scuola (3–4 models)
For each model include:

Schedule and pathway logic (English core + language tracks)

How IB DP would be structured (HL/SL considerations)

How students could pursue IB Bilingual Diploma (what conditions must be met)

Staffing implications (language faculty, TOK/EE, IB coordination)

Student profile it serves best

What makes it distinctive in SF market

Language pathways design
Propose 3 concrete language pathways:

“Strong second language” track

“Second + third language” track

“Italian focus” track (Italian as option, strong but not immersion)
Include: entry points (9th grade vs later), placement approach, support for heritage speakers vs beginners, and outcomes.

Market positioning & messaging
Draft:

1 positioning statement

3 key messages for parents

3 key messages for students

3 proof points we must build (facilities, IB results plan, language outcomes, internships, etc.)

What data we must collect next (action plan)
List the next 10–15 data points to gather (with priority order), plus where to find them (school websites, CAIS, IB directory, Niche/GreatSchools cautiously, tours, parent interviews).

Constraints & quality rules

Be clear where you’re certain vs hypothesizing.

Do not invent facts (tuition, programs, IB status, enrollment). If unknown, mark “Needs verification”.

Focus on SF/Bay Area parent decision drivers: rigor, outcomes, student support, identity, languages, wellbeing, college counseling, facilities, commute, culture.

Keep tone professional, strategic, and actionable.

Output style
Use headings, bullets, and one clean table. Keep it concise but decision-ready.

Optional add-on prompt (if you want it to feel more “La Scuola”)

Paste this after the main prompt:

“Make sure the recommendations align with a school culture that values inquiry, international-mindedness, wellbeing, and language learning, and propose at least two signature programs La Scuola could own (e.g., global citizenship capstone, multilingual debate/diplomacy track, arts/design + IB, internships/community partnerships).”

If you tell me (1) the target opening year you have in mind and (2) whether you’re imagining DP only or DP + another pathway (AP/CP), I can tighten the prompt even more—but the one above will already give you a strong first output.

Post

Building a platform for generative AI applications

Link: https://lnkd.in/gDUcwQ-v

After studying how companies deploy generative AI applications, I noticed many similarities in their platforms. This post outlines these common components, what they do, and implementation considerations.

This post starts from the simplest architecture and progressively add more components.

1. Enhance context input into a model by giving the model access to external data sources and tools for information gathering.

2. Put in guardrails to protect your system and your users.

3. Add model router and gateway to support complex pipelines and add more security.

4. Optimize for latency and costs with cache.

5. Add complex logic and write actions to maximize your system’s capabilities.

I try my best to keep the architecture general, but certain applications might deviate. As always, feedback is appreciated!

#mlengineering #genai #aiapplications


3,984 · 132 comments

Post

To understand the open source AI landscape, I went through the most popular AI repositories on GitHub, categorized them, and studied their growth trajectories. Here are some of the learnings:

https://lnkd.in/exR-PGZX

1. There are 845 generative AI repos with at least 500 stars on GitHub. They are built with contributions from over 20,000 developers, making almost a million commits.

2. I divided the AI stack into four layers: application, application development, model development, and infrastructure. The application and application development layers have seen the most growth in 2023. The infrastructure layer remains more or less the same. Some categories that have seen the most growth include AI interface, inference optimization, and prompt engineering.

3. The landscape exploded in late 2022 but seems to have calmed down since September 2023.

4. While big companies still dominate the landscape, there’s a rise in massively popular software hosted by individuals. Several have speculated that there will soon be billion-dollar one-person companies.

5. China's open source ecosystem is rapidly growing. 6 out of 20 GitHub accounts with the most popular AI repos originate in China, with two from Tsinghua University and two from Shanghai AI Lab.

#generativeai #aiapplications #llmops 

AI stack over time
3,052 · 83 comments

Post

New post: Building LLM applications for production

Link: https://lnkd.in/gi6aKZyJ

I spent the last month talking with companies who are building applications on top of LLMs and realized: it’s easy to build something cool with LLMs, but very hard to build something production-ready with LLMs.

There are several challenges that make productionizing LLM applications hard:

1. The ambiguity of natural languages can make for a delightful user experience but a painful developer experience.

2. The stochastic nature of LLMs can lead to inconsistency in user experience and silent failures.

3. How fast things are evolving makes it very hard to make business decisions: analysis on cost-latency, build (using open source) vs. buy (using paid APIs), prompting vs. finetuning vs. newer techniques needs to be done constantly.

This post discusses these challenges, and what companies are doing to address them. I also discuss more complex applications involving task composability, agent, and control flows.

#llms #promptengineering #mlops #machinelearning #largelanguagemodels

I built a tool to help me stay-up-date with new AI stuff. It's tracking 14K open source repos so far, with contributions from over 145K developers.

Link: https://goodailist.com

It searches for new AI repos every day (based on 123 keywords and topics), surfaces repos that are gaining traction, and automatically categorizes each repo.

It also lets me see where the open source contributors are, so when I travel, I can find folks doing cool stuff in a new city or country.

The annotations are done by AI so they are not super accurate, but they've helped me find some useful stuff for my work!

3mo • 


Had a great time chatting with Lenny Rachitsky on building AI products! Some of the key points I tried to make:

1. Many AI product problems aren’t because of AI. It’s usually because of user experience, data quality, or organizational structure.

A chatbot failed to get traction because their targeted users simply couldn’t type (because their hands were usually busy -- taking care of kids or driving), so showing pre-populated questions and adding a voice option significantly improved traction.

Another team told me their lead scoring model was broken. It turns out that it’s because the marketing team wasn’t asking the right questions to get data.

The biggest product improvements still come from understanding your users, preparing your data, and investing in your team!

2. Senior engineers see the most productivity improvement with AI coding because they have more experience with writing design docs and API specs, which help them write better instructions. 

However, they’re also more resistant to using AI for coding. Senior folks are often more opinionated and get frustrated easily when AI doesn’t do what they want.
   
3. Many teams spend a lot of time debating which tool to use, which can be counter-productive. When teams ask me which of the 2 tools to use, I usually ask 2 questions:

“How much performance improvement will the optional tool give over the less optimal one?”
--> If the improvement is small, then spend less time debating.

“How hard is it to change from one tool to another once you’ve adopted it?”
--> If the tool is new and not yet battle tested, I’d think twice about adopting something that I can’t get out later.

4. Many people know that the most effective way to learn AI is to build with AI. Yet, people keep asking me: “But what should I build?”

We seem to be having an “idea crisis”. We have all these wonderful tools to help us build things, and no idea what to build.

An exercise I often recommend is to spend a week noticing what frustrates you in your daily work, then build small tools to solve those specific pain points.… more

6mo • Edited • 


What people think will improve AI applications vs. what actually does

Made this slide for a talk and folks seemed to like it so I shared it here!

From talking to teams, what I've found to consistently improve application performance include:

1. Talk to users and look at data
Understand how they interact with your application, what features they actually use, where they drop off, etc.

User understanding >> news coverage.

2. Build a more reliable platform
... that allows your team to quickly iterate and improve the application.

Iteration speed >> shiny new tool.

** A reliable platform should also make it easier for you to swap tools in and out as needed!

3. Prepare data better

For many retrieval system, performance improvement can come from:
- better retrieval mechanism
- better data preparation (data is cleaned and processed in a way that makes it easier for the right data to be discovered).

From many use cases that I've seen, the biggest performance boost comes from data preparation, such as better chunking algorithm, rewriting data into Q&A format, or adding the right context/summary/metadata to each chunk.

Data preparation >> vector database debate

** I'm not saying vector databases aren't important. They are! It's just that we should focus on the most impactful axis first.

4.  Optimize for the end-to-end workflow

AI is usually a very small part of the whole system. Constant evaluation of models can take up valuable time that could be spent on optimizing the rest of the system, such as end-to-end latency, systematic evaluation, and data flywheel.

System >> models.

#aiapplications #aiengineering… more

AI x stuff

Visit my website

7mo • 


Very useful tips on tool use and memory from Manus's context engineering blog post. Key takeaways:

1. Reversible compact summary

Most models allow 128K context, which can easily fill up after a few turns when working with data like PDFs or web pages.

When the context gets full, they have to compact it. It’s important to compact the context so that it’s reversible. Eg, removing the content of a file/web page if the path/URL is kept.

2. Tool use

Given how easy it is to add new tools (e.g., with MCP servers), the number of tools a user adds to an agent can explode. Too many tools make it easier for the agent to choose the wrong action, making them dumber.

They caution against removing tools mid-iteration. Instead, you can force an agent to choose certain tools with response prefilling.

Ex: starting your response with

<|im_start|>assistant<tool_call>{"name": “browser_

forces the agent to choose a browser.

Name your tools so that related tools have the same prefix.

Eg: browser tools should start with `browser_`, and command line tools should start with `shell_`

3. Dynamic few shot prompting

They cautioned against using the traditional few shot prompting for agents. Seeing the same few examples again and again will cause the agent to overfit to these examples.

Ex: if you ask the agent to process a batch of 20 resumes, and one example in the prompt visits the job description, the agent might visit the same job description 20 times for these 20 resumes.

Their solution is to introduce small structured variations each time an example is used: different phrasing, minor noise in formatting, etc

Link: https://lnkd.in/gHnWvvcZ

#AIAgents #AIEngineering #AIApplications… more

AI x stuff

7mo • 


I open sourced Sniffly (https://lnkd.in/geEk3HgN), a tool that analyzes Claude Code logs to help me understand my usage patterns and errors.

Key learnings from spending so much time looking at the logs.

1. The biggest type of errors Claude Code made is Content Not Found (20 - 30%). It tries to find files or functions that don't exist.

So I restructured my code base for discoverability, and the average number of steps Claude Code needs for each instruction went from 8 to 7 steps.

2. Traditional metrics of engineering hours/days don’t work for AI. Two metrics I use to evaluate the complexity of a project:

- how many instructions I need to give AI
- how often I have to interrupt it because it goes into the wrong direction

Across my projects, the interruption rate is about 1 in 4 instructions. This means I still need to actively monitor the agent.

3. While most of the time, Claude Code can only go up to 10 steps before I need to interrupt it, it can occasionally go close to 100 steps.

Just a year ago, people told me it was hard to get an agent to go above 5 steps!

Claude Code’s favorite tools are, unsurprisingly, search tools (grep, ls, glob), which make up ⅓ of tool calls.… more

Chip Huyen Executive Top Voice Profile 2ndChip Huyen  • 2nd

AI x stuff

Visit my website

1yr • 


Really enjoyed the conversation with Matt Turck. We covered many topics:

1. Pre-training and post-training
Different models (e.g. Claude and ChatGPT) have fairly similar pre-training since everyone uses the same Internet data and optimizes for the same metric (perplexity), post-training is where these models differ.

2. Perplexity and the end of pre-training?
For a while now, we’ve observed that lowering a language model’s entropy/perplexity leads to better downstream applications’ performance. How long can this trend continue? Is there a lowest possible lower bound for entropy?

3. Sampling
The process of a model picking an output out of so many different outputs, and how it's a quick and easy way to get the performance boost without prompting or finetuning.

4. Evaluating AI systems
While entropy is important for model training, most application developers only care about application performance. What metrics should we use to evaluate an application?

5. System prompt vs. user prompt
And why application developers need to write system prompts in a way that increase application safety.

6. AI agent and planning
One challenge to training a model for planning is in obtaining labeled data. For a given task, we can get humans to annotate the best plan, but what’s efficient for humans isn’t necessarily efficient for AI, and vice versa. For example, summarizing 1000 webpages must be very tedious for humans, but straightforward for an agent that can browse webpages in parallel.

Matt also asked many fun questions that are often taken for granted, such as:

1. What is special about language models that allow them to scale?
2. Why do larger models need more data to train?

Random: I’m super impressed with Matt’s pronunciation of my last name.

https://lnkd.in/gY7tFqAN

I spoke a little too fast, and it was quite an exercise to explain these very technical concepts without a whiteboard. If you find any part of the podcast confusing, the book goes into all these topics in much more detail, with more examples and visualization!

#AIEngineering #AIApplications #MLEngineering… more

AI can get you hired 🤯

My community has been LOVING this trick for standing out.

Here’s how to turn your LinkedIn profile into a ✨killer✨ personal website < 3 minutes
__

1. ☝🏼 Download your LinkedIn profile as a PDF

2. ✌🏼 Go to Replit(.)com + Create App 

3. 🤟🏼 Click Design + drop in the PDF with this prompt in ChatGPT (just tag “Replit”) 
__

“Create a modern, dark-mode personal website using my LinkedIn PDF. Include sections for Home, About, Experience, and Projects. Add smooth scroll navigation, a clean grid layout, my profile image, my updated headline, and space for key stats. Use a deep charcoal background with minimal neon accents. Make it look custom coded and easy to update.”

___

4. Click “Start Designing.”

5. Adjust the content + layout

6. ✅ Hit publish and share live ✨ (that’s it!) 

Congrats 🥳, you’ve created a beautiful, shareable version of your story 🎊

Now here’s a bigger reason why this matters (and why vibe coding is having a moment).

While everyone’s raving over Claude Code, Cursor, Windsurf, and other “AI-first dev tools”, I personally found it intimidating as a non-technical person.

And I found Replit is one of the best places to take my genuine curiosity into an actual *tangible* product (and bring my ideas 💡 → life)

(But if you are *technical*, Replit still works with Claude Code).

I’d love to invite you to build something from zero to 1 (and see how fun it can be!)

Role & context
You are an education strategy analyst helping me explore the feasibility of a future La Scuola International School High School (grades 9–12) in San Francisco. La Scuola is an IB, Reggio-inspired, international community with a strong identity in language learning (Italian heritage, global-mindedness). I’m exploring a model where the main curriculum is in English, with robust options for a second and third language, and Italian offered as an option (not necessarily the primary language of instruction).

Research goal
Produce a market and program feasibility study for an English-dominant IB high school with strong multilingual pathways, designed to compete in the Bay Area independent school market.

Competitors to include (compare directly)

International High School of San Francisco (or International School of San Francisco high school, if applicable)

Lick-Wilmerding High School (Lick)

St. Ignatius College Preparatory (SI)

International School of Silicon Valley (and note if it is now part of another institution / renamed)

“Bilingual Diploma IB” pathway schools (IB Bilingual Diploma approach)

Deliverables (format exactly like this)

Executive summary (1 page)

The 3 most viable HS models for La Scuola

The 3 biggest risks

The 3 strongest differentiators we can own

A preliminary recommendation: Explore / Pilot / Pause with rationale

Competitor comparison table (one row per school)
Include columns:

School type (IB/AP/independent/Catholic/etc.)

Tuition range (if available)

Admissions selectivity (qualitative)

Program signature (what they are known for)

Language offerings (2nd/3rd language depth)

IB status (DP/CP/AP instead)

Student outcomes signals (college counseling reputation, placement patterns, etc.—use only defensible public info)

Strengths vs La Scuola opportunity gaps

Notes + sources to verify (list what to look up)

IB program model options for La Scuola (3–4 models)
For each model include:

Schedule and pathway logic (English core + language tracks)

How IB DP would be structured (HL/SL considerations)

How students could pursue IB Bilingual Diploma (what conditions must be met)

Staffing implications (language faculty, TOK/EE, IB coordination)

Student profile it serves best

What makes it distinctive in SF market

Language pathways design
Propose 3 concrete language pathways:

“Strong second language” track

“Second + third language” track

“Italian focus” track (Italian as option, strong but not immersion)
Include: entry points (9th grade vs later), placement approach, support for heritage speakers vs beginners, and outcomes.

Market positioning & messaging
Draft:

1 positioning statement

3 key messages for parents

3 key messages for students

3 proof points we must build (facilities, IB results plan, language outcomes, internships, etc.)

What data we must collect next (action plan)
List the next 10–15 data points to gather (with priority order), plus where to find them (school websites, CAIS, IB directory, Niche/GreatSchools cautiously, tours, parent interviews).

Constraints & quality rules

Be clear where you’re certain vs hypothesizing.

Do not invent facts (tuition, programs, IB status, enrollment). If unknown, mark “Needs verification”.

Focus on SF/Bay Area parent decision drivers: rigor, outcomes, student support, identity, languages, wellbeing, college counseling, facilities, commute, culture.

Keep tone professional, strategic, and actionable.

Output style
Use headings, bullets, and one clean table. Keep it concise but decision-ready.

Optional add-on prompt (if you want it to feel more “La Scuola”)

Paste this after the main prompt:

“Make sure the recommendations align with a school culture that values inquiry, international-mindedness, wellbeing, and language learning, and propose at least two signature programs La Scuola could own (e.g., global citizenship capstone, multilingual debate/diplomacy track, arts/design + IB, internships/community partnerships).”

If you tell me (1) the target opening year you have in mind and (2) whether you’re imagining DP only or DP + another pathway (AP/CP), I can tighten the prompt even more—but the one above will already give you a strong first output.

Announcing...the top 100 consumer genAI apps, from our team Andreessen Horowitz! We ranked every AI web and mobile product by usage to see what everyday consumer are interacting with. 

Consumer AI is moving fast, with some major updates since our last ranks 6 months ago. Our takeaways: 

1. Creative tools continue to dominate. 52% of top sites are in content generation or editing - including 60% of new entrants! This includes three new video products (Luma AI, Viggle, Vidnoz) and one new music product (Udio). 
Music generator Suno was the "top mover" by number of spots up the list, cracking the top five. 

2. ChatGPT has competition. It remains the top product on web and mobile...but the race to own search / general assistance is heating up! Perplexity broke into the top three on Web, while Anthropic's Claude hit #4. On mobile, Luzia (which claims 45M users) debuted at #25.

3. Bytedance gets in the game. TikTok's parent company has three apps on the mobile list and is pushing into Web with new entrants Gauth (edtech), Coze (bot builder), and Doubao (assistant). The company launched an R&D division focused on gen AI in late 2023.

4. Love it or hate it...this edition of the list saw only one new product category across Web and mobile - aesthetics and dating. On mobile, LooksMax and Umax rate your photos and tell you how to improve, while RIZZ helps respond to dating app messages based on profile and convo screenshots. 

5. Discord drives hyper-growth. Discord servers can be a leading indicator for adoption, as companies "sandbox" or build communities. As of July, we saw 5 new AI cos in Discord's top 100 servers by invite traffic: Viggle, OpenArt AI, Hedra, krea.ai, and Adobe Firefly. Once again, Midjourney ranked #1 in total global Discord invite traffic. 

Check out the full piece here for more of the trends we're seeing in consumer AI: https://lnkd.in/gT6YR64t And if you're building here, reach out!

Excited to announce that Andreessen Horowitz is leading Tradepost’s seed round!

Every platform shift spawns a legendary new set of consumer marketplaces - and AI is no exception.

Tradepost is making everything instantly liquid, starting with tickets...and, the product launches today!

We invested in Tradepost because Tyler Mozeleski (ex-Alt), Alexander Perez (ex-GS), and team are native to how the next gen wants to transact.

It's frictionless and guaranteed - instead of creating + managing a listing, take a picture (or search for an item!), and get a great offer instantly. Marketplaces are hard to cold start, and a core reason for this is demand.

Tradepost has aggregated market makers, who compete to give consumers real-time, fair market offers on their items.

This puts users in control, and makes every scale scam-free.

Check out the Tradepost product (and learn more about the company) here: https://tradepost.co/… more

🚨 Introducing the AI Apps 50: Startup Edition

Ever wondered how startups are spending their money when it comes to AI? Our team at Andreessen Horowitz worked with Mercury to crunch the numbers and rank the top applications by spend.

The list + what we learned from it ⬇️ 

- Horizontal apps have a slight lead over vertical (60% of the list). This includes general assistants (ex. Perplexity) and SIX different meeting support tools (ex. Fyxer AI). But, it also encompasses creative tools and vibe coding tools that are used in roles across orgs.

- Vertical apps can augment human labor...or replace it. We're mostly seeing the former - but five companies on the list allow customers to "hire AI" (ex. Crosby Legal, Cognition, 11x). Labor augmenters mostly assist with customer service, sales, and recruiting.

- Vibe coding has landed in enterprises. It's not just a prosumer trend! Number three on the list, below OpenAI and Anthropic? Replit. Other listmakers in the category include Lovable and Emergent, while Cursor
made the ranks for more technical users.

- Products are making the consumer -> enterprise jump. 12 cos also appeared in our most recent Consumer AI Top 100 - almost all of which started out B2C and have migrated B2B over time. In fact, 70% of listmakers are available for individual use (no enterprise license needed)!

Check out the full report: https://lnkd.in/gmMvfvSv… more

View Olivia Moore’s profile
Olivia Moore Premium Profile 3rd+Olivia Moore  • 3rd+

AI Partner at Andreessen Horowitz

5mo • 


In the AI era, consumer startups are on a new trajectory. The best B2C companies are exceeding 100% net revenue retention - which was previously only possible in B2B. At Andreessen Horowitz, we call this "The Great Expansion." 

In the pre-AI era, B2C companies almost never exceeded 100% NRR. Why? Most users were monetized via a flat monthly subscription or ads. Usage-based pricing was rare. So user retention = revenue retention. And since some users churned, NRR was less than 100% (and often <50%!)

Now, consumer companies are making more money from a user (and even from a cohort, accounting for churn!) over time. How do they do it? There are two major ways, which aren't mutually exclusive - many companies are doing both:

1️⃣ Usage-based pricing. Before AI, most consumer apps had negligible marginal cost - and couldn't really charge more for heavy usage of the product.

With inference, that's changed. Companies now have pricing tiers based on usage + charge more for credits. Power users will spend more and become "whales" - in some cases spending 10x+ more over time (ex. ChatGPT Plus -> Pro). Other examples - SuperGrok, Google AI Ultra, Krea Max.

2️⃣ Enterprise / teams expansion. Many employees want to be the "AI hero" of their company, or they're tasked with finding ways to automate processes / have an AI strategy.

They'll test out consumer tools and then bring them into the workplace, creating massive expansion opportunities. One user can yield a 100+ seat contract. You can charge 1.5x+ more / user for basic (but crucial) security and permissions functionality - Replit, Cursor, ChatGPT, and others have done this successfully!

AI companies also go into enterprise earlier. Canva waited 7 years to debut Teams - this won't fly in 2025! If you don't grab enterprise $, a competitor will. Ex. ElevenLabs already sees substantial rev from enterprise, with features like HIPAA compliance, managed dubbing, etc.

For more examples and our full thesis, check out our post: https://lnkd.in/gbWgsDCJ … more


The Great Expansion: A New Era of Consumer Software | Andreessen HorowitzThe Great Expansion: A New Era of Consumer Software | Andreessen Horowitz

AI can get you hired 🤯

My community has been LOVING this trick for standing out.

Here’s how to turn your LinkedIn profile into a ✨killer✨ personal website < 3 minutes
__

1. ☝🏼 Download your LinkedIn profile as a PDF

2. ✌🏼 Go to Replit(.)com + Create App 

3. 🤟🏼 Click Design + drop in the PDF with this prompt in ChatGPT (just tag “Replit”) 
__

“Create a modern, dark-mode personal website using my LinkedIn PDF. Include sections for Home, About, Experience, and Projects. Add smooth scroll navigation, a clean grid layout, my profile image, my updated headline, and space for key stats. Use a deep charcoal background with minimal neon accents. Make it look custom coded and easy to update.”

___

4. Click “Start Designing.”

5. Adjust the content + layout

6. ✅ Hit publish and share live ✨ (that’s it!) 

Congrats 🥳, you’ve created a beautiful, shareable version of your story 🎊

Now here’s a bigger reason why this matters (and why vibe coding is having a moment).

While everyone’s raving over Claude Code, Cursor, Windsurf, and other “AI-first dev tools”, I personally found it intimidating as a non-technical person.

And I found Replit is one of the best places to take my genuine curiosity into an actual *tangible* product (and bring my ideas 💡 → life)

(But if you are *technical*, Replit still works with Claude Code).

I’d love to invite you to build something from zero to 1 (and see how fun it can be!)

📌 Bring your creative ideas to life here: https://lnkd.in/dNGeWji5

Mical_Neill_Resume_Dealops-2.docx

11 KB

Role & context
You are an education strategy analyst helping me explore the feasibility of a future La Scuola International School High School (grades 9–12) in San Francisco. La Scuola is an IB, Reggio-inspired, international community with a strong identity in language learning (Italian heritage, global-mindedness). I’m exploring a model where the main curriculum is in English, with robust options for a second and third language, and Italian offered as an option (not necessarily the primary language of instruction).

Research goal
Produce a market and program feasibility study for an English-dominant IB high school with strong multilingual pathways, designed to compete in the Bay Area independent school market.

Competitors to include (compare directly)

International High School of San Francisco (or International School of San Francisco high school, if applicable)

Lick-Wilmerding High School (Lick)

St. Ignatius College Preparatory (SI)

International School of Silicon Valley (and note if it is now part of another institution / renamed)

“Bilingual Diploma IB” pathway schools (IB Bilingual Diploma approach)

Deliverables (format exactly like this)

Executive summary (1 page)

The 3 most viable HS models for La Scuola

The 3 biggest risks

The 3 strongest differentiators we can own

A preliminary recommendation: Explore / Pilot / Pause with rationale

Competitor comparison table (one row per school)
Include columns:

School type (IB/AP/independent/Catholic/etc.)

Tuition range (if available)

Admissions selectivity (qualitative)

Program signature (what they are known for)

Language offerings (2nd/3rd language depth)

IB status (DP/CP/AP instead)

Student outcomes signals (college counseling reputation, placement patterns, etc.—use only defensible public info)

Strengths vs La Scuola opportunity gaps

Notes + sources to verify (list what to look up)

IB program model options for La Scuola (3–4 models)
For each model include:

Schedule and pathway logic (English core + language tracks)

How IB DP would be structured (HL/SL considerations)

How students could pursue IB Bilingual Diploma (what conditions must be met)

Staffing implications (language faculty, TOK/EE, IB coordination)

Student profile it serves best

What makes it distinctive in SF market

Language pathways design
Propose 3 concrete language pathways:

“Strong second language” track

“Second + third language” track

“Italian focus” track (Italian as option, strong but not immersion)
Include: entry points (9th grade vs later), placement approach, support for heritage speakers vs beginners, and outcomes.

Market positioning & messaging
Draft:

1 positioning statement

3 key messages for parents

3 key messages for students

3 proof points we must build (facilities, IB results plan, language outcomes, internships, etc.)

What data we must collect next (action plan)
List the next 10–15 data points to gather (with priority order), plus where to find them (school websites, CAIS, IB directory, Niche/GreatSchools cautiously, tours, parent interviews).

Constraints & quality rules

Be clear where you’re certain vs hypothesizing.

Do not invent facts (tuition, programs, IB status, enrollment). If unknown, mark “Needs verification”.

Focus on SF/Bay Area parent decision drivers: rigor, outcomes, student support, identity, languages, wellbeing, college counseling, facilities, commute, culture.

Keep tone professional, strategic, and actionable.

Output style
Use headings, bullets, and one clean table. Keep it concise but decision-ready.

Optional add-on prompt (if you want it to feel more “La Scuola”)

Paste this after the main prompt:

“Make sure the recommendations align with a school culture that values inquiry, international-mindedness, wellbeing, and language learning, and propose at least two signature programs La Scuola could own (e.g., global citizenship capstone, multilingual debate/diplomacy track, arts/design + IB, internships/community partnerships).”

If you tell me (1) the target opening year you have in mind and (2) whether you’re imagining DP only or DP + another pathway (AP/CP), I can tighten the prompt even more—but the one above will already give you a strong first output.

AI can get you hired 🤯

My community has been LOVING this trick for standing out.

Here’s how to turn your LinkedIn profile into a ✨killer✨ personal website < 3 minutes
__

1. ☝🏼 Download your LinkedIn profile as a PDF

2. ✌🏼 Go to Replit(.)com + Create App 

3. 🤟🏼 Click Design + drop in the PDF with this prompt in ChatGPT (just tag “Replit”) 
__

“Create a modern, dark-mode personal website using my LinkedIn PDF. Include sections for Home, About, Experience, and Projects. Add smooth scroll navigation, a clean grid layout, my profile image, my updated headline, and space for key stats. Use a deep charcoal background with minimal neon accents. Make it look custom coded and easy to update.”

___

4. Click “Start Designing.”

5. Adjust the content + layout

6. ✅ Hit publish and share live ✨ (that’s it!) 

Congrats 🥳, you’ve created a beautiful, shareable version of your story 🎊

Now here’s a bigger reason why this matters (and why vibe coding is having a moment).

While everyone’s raving over Claude Code, Cursor, Windsurf, and other “AI-first dev tools”, I personally found it intimidating as a non-technical person.

And I found Replit is one of the best places to take my genuine curiosity into an actual *tangible* product (and bring my ideas 💡 → life)

(But if you are *technical*, Replit still works with Claude Code).

I’d love to invite you to build something from zero to 1 (and see how fun it can be!)
